Why this is the best long-term “free/cheap” design

Fast, mobile-first, SEO-friendly static site on Cloudflare Pages with GitHub integration (push → automatic deploy).

Architecture
Hosting / DNS

Domain purchased annually → DNS hosted in Cloudflare → Cloudflare Pages project connected to GitHub repo. 
Cloudflare Docs
+1

Cloudflare Pages Free plan supports up to 500 builds/month (typical property sites won’t hit this). 
Cloudflare Docs

Frontend stack (static)

Astro (recommended) + Tailwind + component library (your choice)

Astro has a documented Decap CMS integration pattern and supports content collections for typed property data. 
Astro Docs

Build output deployed by Pages (standard npm run build + dist/). 
Cloudflare Docs

Admin portal (owner-friendly)

Decap CMS served from public/admin/ and accessible at https://yourdomain.com/admin/. 
Astro Docs

Owner workflow: login → “Properties” collection → Add/Edit/Hide/Publish → Decap commits to GitHub → Cloudflare rebuilds → site updates.

Decap authentication on Cloudflare Pages (important)

Decap’s GitHub backend needs a server-side OAuth flow; Decap notes Netlify facilitates this by default. 
Decap CMS

To keep everything on Cloudflare, use an external OAuth client (Decap supports this approach). 
Decap CMS

Practical implementation: deploy a small Cloudflare Worker OAuth proxy (template exists) and point Decap backend.base_url to it. 
GitHub

Data model (properties)

Represent each property as a file (Markdown or JSON) in the repo. Minimum fields:

id (uuid), slug

title (e.g., “2BR Townhome – Caledonia”)

status enum: available | pending | rented (drives hide/show)

rent (number), deposit (number)

beds, baths, sqft

addressPublic (optional masked), neighborhood, lat/lng (optional)

features[] (AC, parking, laundry, pets, etc.)

photos[] (paths or URLs)

applyUrl (RentSpree link or internal form route)

applicationFeePaymentLink (Stripe Payment Link URL if needed)

Photos storage guidance

Simplest: store images in repo under public/images/properties/... and let Decap upload there.

Avoid Git LFS: Decap GitHub backend does not support Git LFS, so keep images reasonably compressed. 
Decap CMS

If you expect heavy photo volume, move to Cloudflare R2 for object storage (still cheap/free-tier), but that requires either:

owner pastes R2 image URLs into Decap fields, or

you build a small “media uploader” page for the owner.

Applicant flow (browse → apply → pay)
Browsing UX (mobile-first)

Home: featured available listings + search/filter (beds/baths, max rent, pets, availability)

Listing detail: photo gallery, key facts, amenities, map area (optional), “Apply” + “Contact”

Clear CTA: “Apply now”, “Schedule a tour”, “Ask a question”

Accessibility: keyboard nav, readable contrast, big tap targets, lazy-loaded images

Applications and screening (recommended: outsource)

RentSpree approach:

“Apply” button takes applicant to RentSpree application + screening

Applicant pays screening fee directly (owner avoids collecting + storing sensitive info) 
RentSpree Help Center
+1

RentSpree offers rental application (free) and paid screening components. 
rentspree.com
+1

Application fee / other owner-collected payments

If the owner charges a fee separate from screening:

Use Stripe Payment Links for a no-code hosted checkout page.

Security warning: if you collect high-risk PII (SSN, DOB, full credit history), you become the data custodian. Avoid this unless there’s a business requirement.

Hardening / security checklist

Put /admin behind:

Decap auth (GitHub OAuth via Worker proxy), and optionally

Cloudflare Access policy allowing only the owner’s identity provider/email. 
Cloudflare Docs

Turnstile on every public form endpoint. 
Cloudflare Docs
+1

Rate limit / WAF rules for /api/* and /admin/* (optional)

Use environment secrets in Pages (OAuth client secret, Stripe secret key if using Checkout, Turnstile secret). 
Cloudflare Docs

Engineering implementation plan (what to hand your engineer)
Milestone 1 — Foundation (static site)

Create Astro project + Tailwind + base layout + routing

Implement property list + property detail pages from content collection/files

Implement availability filtering and “Hide rented” logic (status != available)

Add sitemap/robots, metadata, OpenGraph

Milestone 2 — Admin portal (Decap)

Add public/admin/index.html + config.yml

Define collections:

properties

site_pages (About, Contact, FAQ)

settings (application links, fee links, phone/email)

Implement previews (optional)

Implement GitHub OAuth via Cloudflare Worker proxy (decap-proxy pattern)

Add Cloudflare Access policy for /admin (optional but recommended)

Milestone 3 — Apply + Pay flows (outsourced-first)

Add per-property applyUrl and optional stripePaymentLink

UX: “Apply” opens RentSpree (or chosen provider) in-app browser safe

Add confirmation page + FAQ (“What happens after you apply?”)

Milestone 4 — (Optional) Native forms + storage

Pages Functions endpoint(s): /api/apply, /api/contact

Turnstile verification server-side

D1 schema:

applications, messages, audit_log

R2 uploads (signed upload URL flow)

Email notification integration

Milestone 5 — Polish

Lighthouse performance pass (image compression, lazy loading, caching)

Mobile navigation, gallery UX, sticky “Apply” CTA

Analytics (optional)

Claude Code CLI enablement (subagents, skills, slash commands, plugins, hooks)
Recommended structure in your repo

CLAUDE.md: project rules, commands, architecture notes (Claude Code explicitly recommends documenting requirements and using hooks). 
Claude Code

.claude/settings.json: hooks (format on write, run tests, block dangerous edits). 
Claude Code
+2
Claude Code
+2

.claude/commands/: custom slash commands (repeatable workflows). 
Claude Code
+1

.claude/agents/: subagents for focused roles (frontend, CF Workers, security review). 
Claude Code
+1

Optional shared skills under ~/.claude/skills/ or repo-based skill directories (for reusable build standards). 
Claude Code

Suggested subagents (create 4)

frontend-ui: component library, responsive layout, accessibility

cms-admin: Decap config modeling, editorial workflow

cf-worker-backend: Pages Functions, Turnstile verification, D1/R2 bindings

security-review: threat modeling, secrets, auth flows, abuse cases

(Subagents are explicitly designed as specialized assistants with separate context windows.) 
Claude Code

Suggested slash commands (project-scoped)

/spec: write feature spec + acceptance criteria

/cms-model: update Decap config.yml + validate collections

/cf-deploy-check: verify Pages build settings + env vars

/api-apply: generate Pages Function endpoint + Turnstile verification

/stripe-link: generate “owner uses Payment Link” UX text and admin field wiring

/sec-check: run a lightweight security checklist on diffs

(Custom slash commands are file-based and user-invoked.) 
Claude Code

Hooks (deterministic guardrails)

Use hooks to:

auto-run eslint/prettier after edits

prevent commits that include secrets

require updating tests when functions change
(Hooks are shell commands executed at lifecycle points like PreToolUse/PostToolUse.) 
Claude Code
+1

Plugins and marketplaces (team sharing)

If you want standardized behavior across engineers:

package commands/agents/hooks/skills into a plugin and distribute via a marketplace file. 
Claude Code
+2
Claude Code
+2

CLI usage notes

Claude Code CLI supports interactive sessions, “prompt then exit”, resume sessions, updates, and MCP server configuration. 
Claude Code
+1

Cost model (what will actually cost money)

Domain: yearly (your only guaranteed fixed cost)

Cloudflare Pages/Workers/D1/R2: can be $0 if you stay within free tiers (Pages builds, Workers requests, D1 limits, R2 free tier). 
Cloudflare Docs

Cloudflare Docs
+3
Cloudflare Docs
+3

Stripe: per-transaction processing fees (no monthly for Payment Links). 
Stripe Docs
+1

Screening provider (if outsourced): applicant-paid fees are typical (example shown by RentSpree). 
RentSpree Help Center
+1

Option B (more complex): Full custom admin + database

If you don’t want the owner to have GitHub access at all:

Build an authenticated admin app (Cloudflare Access + Pages Functions)

Store properties in D1, images in R2

This becomes a real web app (more code, more security surface, more testing), but still can run on free/cheap Cloudflare primitives. 
Cloudflare Docs

Cloudflare Docs

Cloudflare Docs

Option C (worst for “free forever”): SaaS property management platform

Fastest to deploy, but recurring monthly costs usually appear as soon as you need forms, screening integrations, or more listings.")
